        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is currently considered the most promising anode candidate for room temp. sodium ion batteries because of its relatively high capacity, low cost, and good scalability.  In this work, switchgrass as a biomass example was carbonized under an ultrahigh temp., 2050 °C, induced by Joule heating to create hard carbon anodes for sodium ion batteries.  Switchgrass derived carbon materials intrinsically inherit its three-dimensional porous hierarchical architecture, with an av. interlayer spacing of 0.376 nm.  The larger interlayer spacing than that of graphite allows for the significant Na ion storage performance.  Compared to the sample carbonized under 1000 °C, switchgrass derived carbon at 2050 °C induced an improved initial Coulombic efficiency.  Addnl., excellent rate capability and superior cycling performance are demonstrated for the switchgrass derived carbon due to the unique high temp. treatment.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmL_ip-e763rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhDvoayscsrqQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvF2hu7nK&amp;md5=567543f355beaef8d1a104e02b65ee2c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.07.018"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A high-performance Sodium-ion Battery Enhanced by Macadamia Shell Derived Hard Carbon Anode</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>39</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">489</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">498</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A high-performance sodium-ion battery enhanced by macadamia shell derived hard carbon anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Yuheng; Wang, Yuesheng; Lu, Yaxiang; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Ju</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">39</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">489-498</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIB) have usually been tested in half-cells by cycling between 0-2 V, and is believed to exhibit low rate capability.  However, we find that the specific capacity, the rate performance, and the cycling performance may all be severely underestimated with the traditional half-cell cycling evaluation method, due to premature truncation of part II of the capacity (part I is "sloping", part II is "plateauing", while part III is Na metal deposition).  Here we introduce a sodium-matched SIB full-cell architecture, with newly developed hard carbon derived from macadamia shell (MHC) as anode and Na[Cu1/9Ni2/9Fe1/3Mn1/3]O2 (NCNFM) as the cathode material, with anode/cathode areal capacity ratio of 1.02-1.04.  Our carefully balanced full-cells exhibit a cell-level theor. specific energy of 215 Wh kg-1 at C/10 and 186 Wh kg-1 at 1C based on cathode-active and anode-active material wts., and an outstanding capacity retention of 70% after 1300 cycles ( ∼ 2000h).  Traditional half-cell test (THT) of MHC using superabundant Na metal counter electrode shows only 51.7 mAh g-1 capacity at 1C, and appears to die in no more than 100 h due to low open-circuit voltage slope and large polarization.  A revised half-cell test (RHT) which shows much better agreements with full-cell test results, delivers a specific capacity of 314 mAh g-1, with an initial Coulombic efficiency of ∼ 91.4%, which is comparable to that of graphite anode in lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHl6wt6_FKUbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhDvoayscsrqQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1GjtbnI&amp;md5=8ae9f3066e44cc080d5df2a698d3512a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1039/c6ee03367a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Achieving Superb Sodium Storage Performance on Carbon Anodes Through an Ether-derived Solid Electrolyte Interphase</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Achieving superb sodium storage performance on carbon anodes through an ether-derived solid electrolyte interphase</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jun; Wang, Da-Wei; Lv, Wei; Zhang, Siwei; Liang, Qinghua; Zheng, Dequn; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">370-376</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High sp. surface area carbon (HSSAC) is a class of promising high-capacity anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  A crit. bottleneck of the HSSAC anode, however, is the ultra-low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) in commonly used ester-based electrolytes.  This phenomenon further prohibits improving the specific capacity, long-term stability and rate capability of HSSAC anodes.  This work reports the largely enhanced anode performance of several different HSSAC anodes in ether-based electrolytes.  Very importantly, with the reduced graphene oxide (rGO) anode as one example, the ICE can be as high as 74.6% accompanied by a large reversible specific capacity of 509 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1. 75.2% of the capacity was retained after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1, the specific capacity of the rGO anode can be obtained at 196 mA h g-1.  This extraordinary performance is ascribed to the stable, thin, compact, uniform and ion conducting solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed in an ether-based electrolyte.  Fortunately, this SEI-modifying strategy is generic and is independent of the specific microstructures of HSSAC anodes, indicating a promising avenue for manipulating the SEI on HSSAC anodes through utilizing ether solvents to enable achievement of high ICE for large-capacity HSSAC anodes for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2QXpPrjk4ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limT8eg5-uMow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitV2mtbnN&amp;md5=be5958dc01f38deeacf6a2a0eb32101f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1039/c7ta02515g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.-E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosting the Rate Capability of Hard Carbon With an Ether-based Electrolyte for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A pomegranate-inspired nanoscale design for large-volume-change lithium battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Nian; Lu, Zhenda; Zhao, Jie; McDowell, Matthew T.; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Zhao, Wenting; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">187-192</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Silicon is an attractive material for anodes in energy storage devices, because it has ten times the theor. capacity of its state-of-the-art carbonaceous counterpart.  Silicon anodes can be used both in traditional lithium-ion batteries and in more recent Li-O2 and Li-S batteries as a replacement for the dendrite-forming lithium metal anodes.  The main challenges assocd. with silicon anodes are structural degrdn. and instability of the solid-electrolyte interphase caused by the large vol. change (∼300%) during cycling, the occurrence of side reactions with the electrolyte, and the low volumetric capacity when the material size is reduced to a nanometer scale.  Here, we propose a hierarchical structured silicon anode that tackles all three of these problems.  Our design is inspired by the structure of a pomegranate, where single silicon nanoparticles are encapsulated by a conductive carbon layer that leaves enough room for expansion and contraction following lithiation and delithiation.  An ensemble of these hybrid nanoparticles is then encapsulated by a thicker carbon layer in micrometre-size pouches to act as an electrolyte barrier.  As a result of this hierarchical arrangement, the solid-electrolyte interphase remains stable and spatially confined, resulting in superior cyclability (97% capacity retention after 1,000 cycles).  In addn., the microstructures lower the electrode-electrolyte contact area, resulting in high Coulombic efficiency (99.87%) and volumetric capacity (1,270 mAh cm-3), and the cycling remains stable even when the areal capacity is increased to the level of com. lithium-ion batteries (3.7 mAh cm-2).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDypwI__SZwLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXyCFSZq3eMw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded graphite as superior anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Yang; He, Kai; Zhu, Yujie; Han, Fudong; Xu, Yunhua; Matsuda, Isamu; Ishii, Yoshitaka; Cumings, John; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFEZ8wJYk1irVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXyCFSZq3eMw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVeqs7g%253D&amp;md5=e4bc2edac8d22121e7986e165b7df007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201503221"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Sustainable Route from Biomass Byproduct Okara to High Content Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Sheets for Efficient Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Sustainable Route from Biomass Byproduct Okara to High Content Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Sheets for Efficient Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Tingzhou; Qian, Tao; Wang, Mengfan; Shen, Xiaowei; Xu, Na; Sun, Zhouzhou; Yan, Chenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel concept for synthesizing N-doped carbon sheets (NDCS) is presented which uses okara as the source of both carbon and nitrogen, yielding a higher content of nitrogen (about 9.89 at%) than previous methods.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low-Surface-Area Hard Carbon Anode for Na-Ion Batteries via Graphene Oxide as a Dehydration Agent</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Bommier, Clement; Jian, Zelang; Li, Xin; Carter, Rich; Vail, Sean; Lu, Yuhao; Lee, Jong-Jan; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2626-2631</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are emerging as one of the most promising energy storage technologies, particularly for grid-level applications.  Among anode candidate materials, hard carbon is very attractive due to its high capacity and low cost.  However, hard carbon anodes often suffer a low first-cycle coulombic efficiency and fast capacity fading.  In this study, we discover that doping graphene oxide into sucrose, the precursor for hard carbon, can effectively reduce the sp. surface area of hard carbon to as low as 5.4 m2/g.  We further show that such doping can effectively prevent foaming during caramelization of sucrose and extend the pyrolysis burnoff of sucrose caramel over a wider temp. range.  The obtained low-surface-area hard carbon greatly improves the first-cycle coulombic efficiency from 74% to 83% and delivers a very stable cycle life with 95% of capacity retention after 200 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqaHV_SLIfobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOxK1WcLATNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXks1KlsQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=4b387ca5b76e59789c78130fa5560be4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1039/c4ta05451b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amorphous Monodispersed Hard Carbon Micro-spherules Derived from Biomass as a High Performance Negative Electrode Material for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous monodispersed hard carbon micro-spherules derived from biomass as a high performance negative electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunming; Xu, Shuyin; Wu, Xiaoyan; Yu, Juezhi; Wang, Yuesheng; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale and low-cost elec. energy storage applications in the near future.  Despite this, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, the authors synthesized monodispersed hard carbon spherules (HCS) from an abundant biomass of sucrose, and studied the influence of the carbonization temp. on the microstructure and electrochem. performance.  The initial coulombic efficiency of the HCS was increased to 83% by coating its surface with soft carbon through the pyrolysis of toluene.  The plateau capacity at the low potential region increased with increasing carbonization temp.  The HCS carbonized at 1600° showed the highest plateau capacity (220 mA-h/g) and excellent cycling performance with a capacity retention of 93% after 100 cycles.  When coupled with an air-stable P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 pos. electrode, the full cell exhibited a high initial coulombic efficiency of 76%, a mean operating voltage of 3.5 V and excellent cycling performance.  The theor. energy d. of this system is 200 W-h/kg.  These promising properties are believed to be close to the level required for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1jsHJQCoWPrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOxK1WcLATNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSqs7bK&amp;md5=1d0ab49c7539719d3b644ebc28a2d568</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee24203f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cong, H.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, X.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Graphene-polyaniline Composite Paper for High-performance Supercapacitor</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible graphene-polyaniline composite paper for high-performance supercapacitor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cong, Huai-Ping; Ren, Xiao-Chen; Wang, Ping; Yu, Shu-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Free-standing graphene paper with a gray metallic luster has been fabricated for the first time, by a convenient one-step method on a large scale.  Herein, the assembly of graphene oxide dispersion into ordered paper occurs simultaneously with the chem. redn. of graphene oxide to graphene.  The graphene paper presents the advantages of good flexibility, low wt. (0.2 g cm-3) and high elec. cond. (15 Ω sq-1).                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Freeze-drying for sustainable synthesis of nitrogen doped porous carbon cryogel with enhanced supercapacitor and lithium ion storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ling, Zheng; Yu, Chang; Fan, Xiaoming; Liu, Shaohong; Yang, Juan; Zhang, Mengdi; Wang, Gang; Xiao, Nan; Qiu, Jieshan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">374003/1-374003/11</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">IOP Publishing Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A chitosan (CS) based nitrogen doped carbon cryogel with a high sp. surface area (SSA) has been directly synthesized via a combined process of freeze-drying and high-temp. carbonization without adding any activation agents.  The as-made carbon cryogel demonstrates an SSA up to 1025 m2 g-1 and a high nitrogen content of 5.98 wt%, while its counterpart derived from CS powder only shows an SSA of 26 m2 g-1.  Freeze-drying is a detg. factor for the formation of carbon cryogel with a high SSA, where the CS powder with a size of ca. 200 μm is transformed into the sheet-shaped cryogel with a thickness of 5-8 μm.  The as-made carbon cryogel keeps the sheet-shaped structure and the abundant pores are formed in situ and decorated inside the sheets during carbonization.  The carbon cryogel shows significantly enhanced performance as supercapacitor and lithium ion battery electrodes in terms of capacity and rate capability due to its quasi two-dimensional (2D) structure with reduced thickness.  The proposed method may provide a simple approach to configure 2D biomass-derived advanced carbon materials for energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrSk9yfCxnIQbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHBvpLX7fqNw"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.12.042</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D45%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D220-228%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DR.%2BHao%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DB.%2BJia%26author%3DG.%2BMa%26author%3DD.%2BYu%26author%3DL.%2BGuo%26author%3DS.%2BYang%26title%3DDirect%2BChitin%2BConversion%2Bto%2BN-doped%2BAmorphous%2BCarbon%2BNanofibers%2Bfor%2BHigh-performing%2BFull%2BSodium-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2017.12.042&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b15274&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2017.12.042&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct chitin conversion to N-doped amorphous carbon nanofibers for high-performing full sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hao, Rui; Yang, Yun; Wang, Hua; Jia, Binbin; Ma, Guanshui; Yu, Dandan; Guo, Lin; Yang, Shihe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">45</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">220-228</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Currently, renewable and low-cost electrode materials are being intensively pursued to meet the development of sustainable electrochem. energy-storage systems.  Chitin, which is the second most abundant biopolymer throughout the natural world and can be sourced cheaply from the exoskeletons of arthropods and shells of cephalopods, has many attractive properties such as renewability, nontoxicity, intrinsically fibrous structure and high nitrogen content.  In this study, nitrogen-doped amorphous carbon nanofibers (NACF) fabricated by direct pyrolysis of chitin, were used as the anode material in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) for the first time.  The NACF electrode delivered a high reversible capacity of 320.6 mA h g-1 with excellent rate capability and long cyclability.  The superior electrochem. performance can mainly be attributed to synergistic effects of the unique one-dimensional mesoporous nanofibers facilitating the transmission of electrons/electrolyte, and the N-doped amorphous nanostructure increasing elec. cond. and no. of active sites.  Furthermore, a sodium-ion full cell was constructed by coupling the NACF electrode with a Prussian blue cathode, and it delivered 115 mA h g-1 while retaining 90% of the capacity after 200 cycles.  Our work will hopefully inspire the research community to explore other advanced materials with value-added attributes that can be generated by appropriate treatment of renewable bio-waste.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpMBhBrN1XCULVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHBvpLX7fqNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXltlaisA%253D%253D&amp;md5=96d98c26d48f8bb31d0dda320e5897e5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201706294"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">N-Doping and Defective Nanographitic Domain Coupled Hard Carbon Nanoshells for High Performance Lithium/Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In search of an optimized electrolyte for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ponrouch, Alexandre; Marchante, Elena; Courty, Matthieu; Tarascon, Jean-Marie; Palacin, M. Rosa</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8572-8583</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrolytes are essential for the proper functioning of any battery technol. and the emerging Na-ion technol. is no exception.  Hence, a major focus on battery research is to identify the most appropriate formulation so as to minimize interface reactions and enhance both cell performances and safety aspects.  In order to identify suitable electrolyte formulations for Na-ion chem. we benchmarked various electrolytes contg. diverse solvent mixts. (cyclic, acyclic carbonates, glymes) and Na-based salts having either F-based or perchlorate anions and measured viscosity, ionic cond., and thermal and electrochem. stability.  The binary EC:PC solvent mixt. has emerged as the best solvent formulation and has been used to test the performance of Na/hard carbon cells with both NaClO4 and NaPF6 as dissolved salts.  Hard carbon electrodes having reversible capacities of 200 mA h g-1 with decent rate capability and excellent capacity retention (&gt;180 cycles) were demonstrated.  Moreover, DSC heating curves demonstrated that fully sodiated hard carbon cycled in NaPF6-EC:PC exhibits the highest exothermic onset temp. and nearly the lowest enthalpy of reaction, thus making this electrolyte most attractive for the development of Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp6iY9--X3CQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHBvpLX7fqNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xht1WrsLnE&amp;md5=4cc627e9703d3883d10ee8eccc42e514</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee41379a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ponrouch, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dedryvère, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Monti, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Demet, A.                 10.1039/c3ee41379a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D2361-2369%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DA.%2BPonrouch%26author%3DR.%2BDedryv%25C3%25A8re%26author%3DD.%2BMonti%26author%3DA.%2BE.%2BDemet%26author%3DJ.%2BM.%2BA.%2BMba%26author%3DL.%2BCroguennec%26author%3DC.%2BMasquelier%26author%3DP.%2BJohansson%26author%3DM.%2BR.%2BPalac%25C3%25ADn%26title%3DTowards%2BHigh%2BEnergy%2BDensity%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%2BThrough%2BElectrolyte%2BOptimization%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc3ee41379a&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b15274&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc3ee41379a&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Towards high energy density sodium ion batteries through electrolyte optimization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ponrouch, Alexandre; Dedryvere, Remi; Monti, Damien; Demet, Atif E.; Ateba Mba, Jean Marcel; Croguennec, Laurence; Masquelier, Christian; Johansson, Patrik; Palacin, M. Rosa</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2361-2369</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A comprehensive study is reported entailing optimization of sodium ion electrolyte formulation and compatibility studies with pos. and neg. electrode materials.  EC:PC:DMC and EC:PC:DME were found to exhibit optimum ionic conductivities and lower viscosities.  Yet, hard carbon neg. electrode materials tested in such electrolytes exhibit significant differences in performance, rooted in the different resistivity of the SEI, which results in too large polarization and concomitant loss of capacity at low potentials when DME is used as a co-solvent.  EC0.45:PC0.45:DMC0.1 was found to be the optimum compn. resulting in good rate capability and high capacity upon sustained cycling for hard carbon electrodes.  Its compatibility with pos. Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) electrodes was also confirmed, which led to the assembly of full Na-ion cells displaying an operation voltage of 3.65 V, very low polarization and excellent capacity retention upon cycling with ca. 97 mA h g-1 of NVPF after more than 120 cycles together with satisfactory coulombic efficiency (&gt;98.5%) and very good power performance.  Such values lead to energy densities comparable to those of the current state-of-the-art lithium-ion technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWWc8cwpdbDbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_amgDNTzYvA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOisr7M&amp;md5=3b08f3921d6438d33b14eb6e5184904a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.-U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Hong, Jihyun; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Jinsoo; Hwang, Insang; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">534-541</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_amgDNTzYvA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref59'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1021/acscentsci.5b00328"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seh, Z. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Highly Reversible Room-Temperature Sodium Metal Anode</span>. <i>ACS Cent. Sci.ACS Central Science</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">449</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">455</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acscentsci.5b00328</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D1%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D449-455%26journal%3DACS%2BCent.%2BSci.ACS%2BCentral%2BScience%26author%3DZ.%2BW.%2BSeh%26author%3DJ.%2BSun%26author%3DY.%2BSun%26author%3DY.%2BCui%26title%3DA%2BHighly%2BReversible%2BRoom-Temperature%2BSodium%2BMetal%2BAnode%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facscentsci.5b00328&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b15274&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facscentsci.5b00328&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Highly Reversible Room-Temperature Sodium Metal Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Seh, Zhi Wei; Sun, Jie; Sun, Yongming; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Central Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">449-455</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACSCII</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2374-7951</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to its low cost and high natural abundance, sodium metal is among the most promising anode materials for energy storage technologies beyond lithium ion batteries.  However, room-temp. sodium metal anodes suffer from poor reversibility during long-term plating and stripping, mainly due to formation of nonuniform solid electrolyte interphase as well as dendritic growth of sodium metal.  Herein it is reported for the first time that a simple liq. electrolyte, sodium hexafluorophosphate in glymes (mono-, di-, and tetraglyme), can enable highly reversible and nondendritic plating-stripping of sodium metal anodes at room temp.  High av. Coulombic efficiencies of 99.9% were achieved over 300 plating-stripping cycles at 0.5 mA cm-2.  The long-term reversibility was found to arise from the formation of a uniform, inorg. solid electrolyte interphase made of sodium oxide and sodium fluoride, which is highly impermeable to electrolyte solvent and conducive to nondendritic growth.  As a proof of concept, a room-temp. sodium-sulfur battery is demonstrated using this class of electrolytes, paving the way for the development of next-generation, sodium-based energy storage technologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdqXOWzEW74bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_amgDNTzYvA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVGmtrfL&amp;md5=6155e3c781a24b8340081c2ad4444616</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref60'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201801389"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Porous Network of Bismuth Used as the Anode Material for High-Energy-Density Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>57</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4687</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4691</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Porous Network of Bismuth Used as the Anode Material for High-Energy-Density Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lei, Kaixiang; Wang, Chenchen; Liu, Luojia; Luo, Yuwen; Mu, Chaonan; Li, Fujun; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">57</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4687-4691</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (KIBs) are plagued by a lack of materials for reversible accommodation of the large-sized K+ ion.  Herein we present, the Bi anode in combination with the dimethoxyethane-(DME) based electrolyte to deliver a remarkable capacity of ca. 400 mAh g-1 and long cycle stability with three distinct two-phase reactions of Bi↔ KBi2↔K3Bi2↔K3Bi.  These are ascribed to the gradually developed three-dimensional (3D) porous networks of Bi, which realizes fast kinetics and tolerance of its vol. change during potassiation and depotassiation.  The porosity is linked to the unprecedented movement of the surface Bi atoms interacting with DME mols., as suggested by DFT calcns.  A full KIB of Bi//DME-based electrolyte//Prussian blue of K0.72Fe[Fe(CN)6] is demonstrated to present large energy d. of 108.1 Wh kg-1 with av. discharge voltage of 2.8 V and capacity retention of 86.5 % after 350 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGow7ZpTRkXZvbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_amgDNTzYvA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXkslCnt7Y%253D&amp;md5=5bba36fc43196668038c56003b44bf12</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref61'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Henderson, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sushko, M.                 10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.034</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D19%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D279-288%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DL.%2BXiao%26author%3DY.%2BCao%26author%3DW.%2BHenderson%26author%3DM.%2BL.%2BSushko%26author%3DY.%2BShao%26author%3DJ.%2BXiao%26author%3DW.%2BWang%26author%3DM.%2BH.%2BEngelhard%26author%3DZ.%2BNie%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26title%3DHard%2BCarbon%2BNanoparticles%2Bas%2BHigh-capacity%252C%2BHigh-stability%2BAnodic%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BNa-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2015.10.034&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b15274&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2015.10.034&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbon nanoparticles as high-capacity, high-stability anodic materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Lifen; Cao, Yuliang; Henderson, Wesley A.; Sushko, Maria L.; Shao, Yuyan; Xiao, Jie; Wang, Wei; Engelhard, Mark H.; Nie, Zimin; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">279-288</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon nanoparticles (HCNP) were synthesized by the pyrolysis of a polyaniline precursor.  The measured Na+ cation diffusion coeff. (10-13-10-15 cm2 s-1) in the HCNP obtained at 1150 °C is two orders of magnitude lower than that of Li+ in graphite (10-10-10-13 cm2 s-1), indicating that reducing the carbon particle size is very important for improving electrochem. performance.  These measurements also enable a clear visualization of the stepwise reaction phases and rate changes which occur throughout the insertion/extn. processes in HCNP, The electrochem. measurements also show that the nano-sized HCNP obtained at 1150 °C exhibited higher practical capacity at voltages lower than 1.2 V (vs. Na/Na+), as well as a prolonged cycling stability, which is attributed to an optimum spacing of 0.366 nm between the graphitic layers and the nano particular size resulting in a low-barrier Na+ cation insertion.  These results suggest that HCNP is a very promising high-capacity/stability anode for low cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0215ZE-6YJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liZwFtyoa0bVA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVaqtrrE&amp;md5=93cb764059ea5aaa3841222611c03416</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref62'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit62" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b05566"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Savilov, S. X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitive Na-Ion Storage Boosts High Rate and Areal Capacity of Self-Branched 2D Layered Metal Chalcogenide Nanoarrays</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">10211</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">10219</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.6b05566</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D10211-10219%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DD.%2BChao%26author%3DP.%2BLiang%26author%3DZ.%2BChen%26author%3DL.%2BBai%26author%3DH.%2BShen%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BXia%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DS.%2BV.%2BSavilov%26author%3DJ.%2BLin%26author%3DZ.%2BX.%2BShen%26title%3DPseudocapacitive%2BNa-Ion%2BStorage%2BBoosts%2BHigh%2BRate%2Band%2BAreal%2BCapacity%2Bof%2BSelf-Branched%2B2D%2BLayered%2BMetal%2BChalcogenide%2BNanoarrays%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.6b05566&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b15274&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.6b05566&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Na-Ion Storage Boosts High Rate and Areal Capacity of Self-Branched 2D Layered Metal Chalcogenide Nanoarrays</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Liang, Pei; Chen, Zhen; Bai, Linyi; Shen, He; Liu, Xiaoxu; Xia, Xinhui; Zhao, Yanli; Savilov, Serguei V.; Lin, Jianyi; Shen, Ze Xiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10211-10219</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundant reserve and low cost of sodium have provoked tremendous evolution of Na-ion batteries (SIBs) in the past few years, but their performances are still limited by either the specific capacity or rate capability.  Attempts to pursue high rate ability with maintained high capacity in a single electrode remains even more challenging.  Here, an elaborate self-branched 2-dimensional SnS2 (B-SnS2) nanoarray electrode is designed by a facile hot bath method for Na storage.  This interesting electrode exhibits areal reversible capacity of ∼3.7 mAh/cm2 (900 mAh/g) and rate capability of 1.6 mAh/cm2 (400 mAh/g) at 40 mA/cm2 (10 A/g).  Improved extrinsic pseudocapacitive contribution is demonstrated as the origin of fast kinetics of an alloying-based SnS2 electrode.  Sodiation dynamics anal. based on 1st-principles calcns., ex-situ HRTEM, in situ impedance, and in situ Raman technologies verify the S-edge effect on the fast Na+ migration and reversible and sensitive structure evolution during high-rate charge/discharge.  The excellent alloying-based pseudocapacitance and unsatd. edge effect enabled by self-branched surface nanoengineering could be a promising strategy for promoting development of SIBs with both high capacity and high rate response.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®"         </p><ol id="rightTab-references" class="useLabel"><li id="rightTab-ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref1" class="rightTabRefNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit1" data-doi="10.1021/ja3091438"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goodenough, J. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, K.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Li-Ion Rechargeable Battery: A Perspective</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>135</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1167</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1176</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja3091438</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Li-Ion Rechargeable Battery: A Perspective</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Goodenough, John B.; Park, Kyu-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">135</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1167-1176</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Each cell of a battery stores elec. energy as chem. energy in two electrodes, a reductant (anode) and an oxidant (cathode), sepd. by an electrolyte that transfers the ionic component of the chem. reaction inside the cell and forces the electronic component outside the battery.  The output on discharge is an external electronic current I at a voltage V for a time Δt.  The chem. reaction of a rechargeable battery must be reversible on the application of a charging I and V.  Crit. parameters of a rechargeable battery are safety, d. of energy that can be stored at a specific power input and retrieved at a specific power output, cycle and shelf life, storage efficiency, and cost of fabrication.  Conventional ambient-temp. rechargeable batteries have solid electrodes and a liq. electrolyte.  The pos. electrode (cathode) consists of a host framework into which the mobile (working) cation is inserted reversibly over a finite solid-soln. range.  The solid-soln. range, which is reduced at higher current by the rate of transfer of the working ion across electrode/electrolyte interfaces and within a host, limits the amt. of charge per electrode formula unit that can be transferred over the time Δt = Δt(I).  Moreover, the difference between energies of the LUMO and the HOMO of the electrolyte, i.e., electrolyte window, dets. the max. voltage for a long shelf and cycle life.  The max. stable voltage with an aq. electrolyte is 1.5 V; the Li-ion rechargeable battery uses an org. electrolyte with a larger window, which increase the d. of stored energy for a given Δt.  Anode or cathode electrochem. potentials outside the electrolyte window can increase V, but they require formation of a passivating surface layer that must be permeable to Li+ and capable of adapting rapidly to the changing electrode surface area as the electrode changes vol. during cycling.  A passivating surface layer adds to the impedance of the Li+ transfer across the electrode/electrolyte interface and lowers the cycle life of a battery cell.  Moreover, formation of a passivation layer on the anode robs Li from the cathode irreversibly on an initial charge, further lowering the reversible Δt.  These problems plus the cost of quality control of manufg. plague development of Li-ion rechargeable batteries that can compete with the internal combustion engine for powering elec. cars and that can provide the needed low-cost storage of elec. energy generated by renewable wind and/or solar energy.  Chemists are contributing to incremental improvements of the conventional strategy by investigating and controlling electrode passivation layers, improving the rate of Li+ transfer across electrode/electrolyte interfaces, identifying electrolytes with larger windows while retaining a Li+ cond. σLi &gt; 10-3 S cm-1, synthesizing electrode morphologies that reduce the size of the active particles while pinning them on current collectors of large surface area accessible by the electrolyte, lowering the cost of cell fabrication, designing displacement-reaction anodes of higher capacity that allow a safe, fast charge, and designing alternative cathode hosts.  However, new strategies are needed for batteries that go beyond powering hand-held devices, such as using electrode hosts with two-electron redox centers; replacing the cathode hosts by materials that undergo displacement reactions (e.g. sulfur) by liq. cathodes that may contain flow-through redox mols., or by catalysts for air cathodes; and developing a Li+ solid electrolyte separator membrane that allows an org. and aq. liq. electrolyte on the anode and cathode sides, resp.  Opportunities exist for the chemist to bring together oxide and polymer or graphene chem. in imaginative morphologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqKg_SkQGkZrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh3pjfNCA0PHg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXktFSisw%253D%253D&amp;md5=9b3d655905f4b3dc188e98f8370452df</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow carbon nanowires were prepd. by pyrolysis of a hollow polyaniline nanowire precursor.                         rightTab-cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New Mechanistic Insights on Na-Ion Storage in Nongraphitizable Carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bommier, Clement; Surta, Todd Wesley; Dolgos, Michelle; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5888-5892</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nongraphitizable carbon, also known as hard carbon, is considered one of the most promising anodes for the emerging Na-ion batteries.  The current mechanistic understanding of Na-ion storage in hard carbon is based on the "card-house" model first raised in the early 2000s.  This model describes that Na-ion insertion occurs first through intercalation between graphene sheets in turbostratic nanodomains, followed by Na filling of the pores in the carbon structure.  We tried to test this model by tuning the sizes of turbostratic nanodomains but revealed a correlation between the structural defects and Na-ion storage.  Based on our exptl. data, we propose an alternative perspective for sodiation of hard carbon that consists of Na-ion storage at defect sites, by intercalation and last via pore-filling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqegbEbsDPzrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZa0CA-7bGLg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a top alternative to Li-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of Na-bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  However, the development of anode materials for SIBs to date was mainly limited to carbonaceous materials with minimal research devoted to high capacity alloy-based materials.  An Sb/C electrode with ∼30 nm Sb nanoparticles (NPs) uniformly encapsulated in interconnecting 1-dimensional (1D) 400 nm C fibers (denoted as SbNP@C) was fabricated using a simple and scalable electrospinning method.  This binder-free, current collector-free SbNP@C electrode demonstrated high capacity and stable long-term cycling performance at various current densities.  The SbNP@C electrode showed an initial total capacity of 422 mA-h/gelectrode and retained 350 mA-h/gelectrode after 300 deep charge-discharge cycles under 100 mA/gSb.  Also, because of the efficient 1-dimensional Na-ion transport pathway and the highly conductive network of SbNP@C, the electrode preserved high overall capacities even when cycled at high currents, extending its usability to high power applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCf3y1wC4rXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTUWJVO2rBRg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">In the current research project, we have prepd. a novel Sb@C nanosphere anode with biomimetic yolk-shell structure for Li/Na-ion batteries via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement route.  The yolk-shell microstructure consists of Sb hollow yolk completely protected by a well-conductive carbon thin shell.  The substantial void space in the these hollow Sb@C yolk-shell particles allows for the full vol. expansion of inner Sb while maintaining the framework of the Sb@C anode and developing a stable SEI film on the outside carbon shell.  As for Li-ion battery anode, they displayed a large specific capacity (634 mAh/g), high rate capability (specific capabilities of 622, 557, 496, 439, and 384 mAh/g at 100, 200, 500, 1000, and 2000 mA/g, resp.) and stable cycling performance (a specific capacity of 405 mAh/g after long 300 cycles at 1000 mA/g).                         rightTab-cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red Phosphorus-Single-Walled Carbon Nanotube Composite as a Superior Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Wen, Yang; Fan, Xiulin; Gao, Tao; Han, Fudong; Luo, Chao; Liou, Sz-Chian; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as a top alternative to Li ion batteries due to the earth abundance and low cost of Na compared with Li.  Among all proposed anode materials for SIBs, red P is a very promising candidate because it has the highest theor. capacity (∼2600 mA-h g-1).  A red P-single-walled C nanotube (denoted as red P-SWCNT) composite, in which red P is uniformly distributed between tangled SWCNTs bundles, is fabricated by a modified vaporization-condensation method.  Benefiting from the nondestructive prepn. process, the highly conductive and mech. strong SWCNT network is preserved, which enhances the cond. of the composite and stabilizes the solid electrolyte interphase.  As a result, the red P-SWCNT composite presents a high overall Na storage capacity (∼700 mA-h g-1composite at 50 mA/gcomposite), fast rate capability (∼300 mA-h g-1composite at 2000 mA/gcomposite), and stable long-term cycling performance with 80% capacity retention after 2000 sodiation-desodiation cycles.  The red P-SWCNT composite fabricated by the vaporization-condensation method significantly extends the cycling stability of P/C composite from current ∼100 cycles to ∼2000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqd3GxgIxmfmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTUWJVO2rBRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjvVOhs7c%253D&amp;md5=6ba87307633bf69051e0eb4e034c85a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1021/nl303823k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Langrock, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zachariah, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nano-Sn/C composites are ideal anode materials for high energy and power d. Li-ion batteries.  However, because of the low m.p. of Sn and the tendency of grain growth, esp. during high temp. carbonization, it was a significant challenge to create well-dispersed ultra-small Sn nanoparticles within a C matrix.  The authors demonstrate an aerosol spray pyrolysis technique, as a facile and scalable method, to synthesize a nano-Sn/C composite with uniformly dispersed 10 nm nano-Sn within a spherical C matrix.  The discharge capacity of nano-Sn/C composite sphere anodes maintains the initial capacity of 710 mA-h/g after 130 cycles at 0.25 C.  The nano-Sn/C composite sphere anodes can provide ∼600 mA-h/g even at a high rate of 20 C.  Such high rate performance for Sn anodes was not reported previously.  The exceptional performance of the nano-Sn/C composite is attributed to the unique nano-Sn/C structure: (a) C matrix offers mech. support to accommodate the stress assocd. with the large vol. change of nano-Sn, thus alleviating pulverization; (b) the C matrix prevents Sn nanoparticle agglomeration upon prolonged cycling; and (c) C network provides continuous path for Li ions and electrons inside the nano-Sn/C composite spheres.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrLYyFaDGc2HbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTUWJVO2rBRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhslGgtw%253D%253D&amp;md5=eb1dcc0d9d76d861eb8b2a90655d874b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200346"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Performance of Porous Carbon/Tin Composite Anodes for Sodium-Ion and Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. performance of mesoporous carbon (C)/tin (Sn) anodes in Na-ion and Li-ion batteries is systematically investigated.  The mesoporous C/Sn anodes in a Na-ion battery shows similar cycling stability but lower capacity and poorer rate capability than that in a Li-ion battery.  The desodiation potentials of Sn anodes are approx. 0.21 V lower than delithiation potentials.  The low capacity and poor rate capability of C/Sn anode in Na-ion batteries is mainly due to the large Na-ion size, resulting in slow Na-ion diffusion and large vol. change of porous C/Sn composite anode during alloy/dealloy reactions. Mn- and Fe-based cathode materials, such as LiMn2O4 and LiFePO4, are used in large-scale batteries for elec. vehicles.  Mn and Fe are abundant elements in the Earth's crust, but Li is not.  In contrast to Li, Na is an attractive charge carrier from elemental abundance.  Recently, some layered materials, where Na can be electrochem. and reversibly extd./inserted, have been reported.         </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V. We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. carbonyl compds. represent a promising class of electrode materials for secondary batteries; however, the storage mechanism still remains unclear.  We take Na2C6H2O4 as an example to unravel the mechanism.  It consists of alternating Na-O octahedral inorg. layer and π-stacked benzene org. layer in spatial sepn., delivering a high reversible capacity and first coulombic efficiency.  The expt. and calcn. results reveal that the Na-O inorg. layer provides both Na+ ion transport pathway and storage site, whereas the benzene org. layer provides electron transport pathway and redox center. Peter; Hazelton, Michael; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
